Marijuana arrests decreased by 56% for Whites, 39% for Hispanics, and	51% for Blacks. The marijuana arrest rate for Blacks (233 per 100,000) was nearly double that of Whites (118 per 100,000) in 2017.		Arrest rates still higher for African Americans.
Colorado State Patrol: Summonses in which alcohol was the only substance decreased by 949 (‚Äê20%). The number of summonses in which marijuana or marijuana‚Äêin‚Äêcombination was recorded increased by 35 (5%) between 2014 and 2017.
Important. Society is not treating drugged driving like drunk driving. Fewer convictions.		These findings suggest that convictions are more common at the per se level for alcohol and at the permissible inference level for Delta‚Äê9 THC.
In April 2018, there were 88,946 individuals registered as medical marijuana cardholders. The most common conditions reported were severe pain (93%), muscle spasms (31%), and severe nausea (14%).
Marijuana tax revenue remains about 1.7 % of tax revenue for state.		Total revenue from taxes, licenses, and fees increased from $67,594,325 in 2014 to $247,368,474 in 2017 (+266%).
In May 2018, 3,101 licensed marijuana businesses were registered in Colorado. Nearly 70% of the licenses for marijuana businesses were concentrated in the counties of Denver (1,226), El Paso (370), Pueblo (303), and Boulder (216).
Important benchmark: Of parents with children ages 1‚Äì14 who responded to the survey, 6.9% reported some type of marijuana product around the house.
Note that Senate Bill 12‚Äê046 and House Bill 12‚Äê1345 targeted reform of ‚Äúzero tolerance‚Äù policies in schools, and appear to have decreased expulsions, suspensions, and referrals to law enforcement.
School discipline data for 2017‚Äê18 indicated that marijuana accounted for 22% of all expulsions and 24% of all law enforcement referrals in Colorado public schools.
Data from the Colorado Department of Education show that that drug suspension rates increased from 391 (per 100,000 registered students) in the 2008‚Äê09 school year to 551 in 2010‚Äê 11. The drug suspension rate fluctuated somewhat since then and was 507 in the 2017‚Äê18 school year.
The proportion of 15‚Äê to 17‚Äêyear‚Äêolds testing positive one or two times went down slightly, from 26% in 2012 to 25% in 2014, while those testing positive three or more times increased from 23% to 25%.
Data from the state Division of Probation Services indicated that the proportion of 10‚Äê to 14‚Äê year‚Äêolds testing positive for THC one or two times increased from 19% in 2012 to 23% in 2014, while the proportion testing positive three or more times increased from 18% to 25%.
More good news, the number of juvenile marijuana arrests decreased 16%, from 3,168 in 2012 to 2,655 in 2017. This is different to other studies that have shown an increase in youth arrests, especially among Hispanic and African American youth.
Study sites Healthy Kids Colorado Survey regarding youth marijuana use rates. Good news, but problems with HKCS study. Leaves out major areas like Jefferson County.
The number of calls to poison control mentioning human marijuana exposure increased over the past 10 years. There were 45 calls in 2006 and 222 in 2017. Between 2014 and 2017, the frequency of calls reporting human marijuana exposure stabilized.
The period of retail commercialization showed an increase in emergency department visits, from 739 per 100,000 ED visits (2010‚Äì2013) to 913 per 100,000 ED visits (January 2014‚ÄìSeptember 2015).
Hospitalization rates (per 100,000 hospitalizations) with possible marijuana exposures, diagnoses, or billing codes increased from 803 per 100,000 before commercialization (2001‚Äê2009) to 2,696 per 100,000 after commercialization (January 2014‚ÄêSeptember 2015).
Reported 30‚Äêday marijuana use by adults ages 26 years and older increased from 5% in 2005/06 to 14% in 2015/16.
Adults ages 18‚Äê25 reported the highest past 30‚Äêday usage rates (29.2%), followed by 26‚Äê34 year olds (26.4%), 35‚Äê64 year olds (12.5%), and those 65 years and older (5.6%).
Males have significantly higher past 30‚Äêday use (19.8%) than females (11.2%).
More adults using marijuana: 		In 2017, 15.5% of adults reported marijuana use in the past 30 days, compared to 13.6% in 2014, a significant increase. Also, in 2017, 7.6% reported daily or near daily use. This compares to 6.0% in 2014, a significant increase.
More marijuana being shipped out to other states. What about states' rights?		The number of seizures for Colorado‚Äêsourced marijuana reported to EPIC increased from 286 in 2012 to 608 in 2017.
More marijuana being illegally grown on public land: 		The number of plants seized on public lands increased. There were 80,926 plants seized in 2017, up 73% from 46,662 in 2012.
More people on probation using marijuana.		The proportion of 18 to 25 year‚Äêold probationers testing positive for THC increased, from 32% in 2012 and 41% in 2017. The proportion of 36 and older probationers testing positive for THC also increased, from 14% in 2012 to 21% in 2017.
A 2017 survey conducted by the Colorado Department of Public Health and Environment found that 3.0% of adults reported driving within two‚Äêto‚Äêthree hours of using marijuana in the past‚Äê30 days, while 19.7% of recent marijuana users reported this behavior.
Marijuana related traffic fatalities still a major problem:		The number of fatalities with cannabinoid‚Äêonly or cannabinoid‚Äêin‚Äêcombination	positive drivers increased 153%, from 55 in 2013 to 139 in 2017.
While overall DUIs are down,		The prevalence of marijuana or marijuana‚Äêin‚Äêcombination identified by Patrol officers as the impairing substance increased from 12% of all DUIs in 2014 to 15% in 2017.
Organized crime court filings up big in Colorado. 		In terms of organized crime, the number of court filings charged with the Colorado Organized Crime Control Act (C.R.S.18‚Äê17.104) that were linked to some marijuana charge increased from 31 in 2012 to 119 in 2017.
